# SLATEC Routines: Alphabetical Index

[A](#alpha-a) [B](#alpha-b) [C](#alpha-c) [D](#alpha-d) [E](#alpha-e) [F](#alpha-f) [G](#alpha-g) [H](#alpha-h) [I](#alpha-i) [J](#alpha-j) [K](#alpha-k) [L](#alpha-l) [M](#alpha-m) [N](#alpha-n) [O](#alpha-o) [P](#alpha-p) [Q](#alpha-q) [R](#alpha-r) [S](#alpha-s) [T](#alpha-t) [U](#alpha-u) [V](#alpha-v) [W](#alpha-w) [X](#alpha-x) [Y](#alpha-y) [Z](#alpha-z)

## <a id="alpha-a"></a>A

| Routine | Family | Role | Purpose | Coverage |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| <a id="routine-aaaaaa"></a>[AAAAAA](routine-details.md#routine-aaaaaa) | Shared numerical utilities | user_callable | SLATEC Common Mathematical Library disclaimer and version. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-acos"></a>[ACOS](routine-details.md#routine-acos) | Elementary and transcendental functions | source_only_unclassified | Compute the arccosine. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-acosh"></a>[ACOSH](routine-details.md#routine-acosh) | Elementary and transcendental functions | user_callable | Compute the arc hyperbolic cosine. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-ai"></a>[AI](routine-details.md#routine-ai) | Special functions | user_callable | Evaluate the Airy function. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-aie"></a>[AIE](routine-details.md#routine-aie) | Special functions | user_callable | Calculate the Airy function for a negative argument and an exponentially scaled Airy function for a non-negative argument. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-albeta"></a>[ALBETA](routine-details.md#routine-albeta) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute the natural logarithm of the complete Beta function. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-algams"></a>[ALGAMS](routine-details.md#routine-algams) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute the logarithm of the absolute value of the Gamma function. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-ali"></a>[ALI](routine-details.md#routine-ali) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute the logarithmic integral. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-alngam"></a>[ALNGAM](routine-details.md#routine-alngam) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute the logarithm of the absolute value of the Gamma function. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-alnrel"></a>[ALNREL](routine-details.md#routine-alnrel) | Elementary and transcendental functions | user_callable | Evaluate ln(1+X) accurate in the sense of relative error. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-alog"></a>[ALOG](routine-details.md#routine-alog) | Elementary and transcendental functions | source_only_unclassified | Compute the natural logarithm of a number. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-alog10"></a>[ALOG10](routine-details.md#routine-alog10) | Elementary and transcendental functions | source_only_unclassified | Compute the common base 10 logarithm. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-asin"></a>[ASIN](routine-details.md#routine-asin) | Elementary and transcendental functions | source_only_unclassified | Compute the arcsine. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-asinh"></a>[ASINH](routine-details.md#routine-asinh) | Elementary and transcendental functions | user_callable | Compute the arc hyperbolic sine. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-asyik"></a>[ASYIK](routine-details.md#routine-asyik) | Special functions | subsidiary | Subsidiary to BESI and BESK | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-asyjy"></a>[ASYJY](routine-details.md#routine-asyjy) | Special functions | subsidiary | Subsidiary to BESJ and BESY | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-atan"></a>[ATAN](routine-details.md#routine-atan) | Elementary and transcendental functions | source_only_unclassified | Compute the arctangent. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-atan2"></a>[ATAN2](routine-details.md#routine-atan2) | Elementary and transcendental functions | source_only_unclassified | Compute the arctangent in the proper quadrant. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-atanh"></a>[ATANH](routine-details.md#routine-atanh) | Elementary and transcendental functions | user_callable | Compute the arc hyperbolic tangent. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-avint"></a>[AVINT](routine-details.md#routine-avint) | Numerical quadrature | user_callable | Integrate a function tabulated at arbitrarily spaced abscissas using overlapping parabolas. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |

## <a id="alpha-b"></a>B

| Routine | Family | Role | Purpose | Coverage |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| <a id="routine-bakvec"></a>[BAKVEC](routine-details.md#routine-bakvec) | Eigenvalue problems | user_callable | Form the eigenvectors of a certain real non-symmetric tridiagonal matrix from a symmetric tridiagonal matrix output from FIGI. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-balanc"></a>[BALANC](routine-details.md#routine-balanc) | Eigenvalue problems | user_callable | Balance a real general matrix and isolate eigenvalues whenever possible. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-balbak"></a>[BALBAK](routine-details.md#routine-balbak) | Eigenvalue problems | user_callable | Form the eigenvectors of a real general matrix from the eigenvectors of matrix output from BALANC. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bandr"></a>[BANDR](routine-details.md#routine-bandr) | Eigenvalue problems | user_callable | Reduce a real symmetric band matrix to symmetric tridiagonal matrix and, optionally, accumulate orthogonal similarity transformations. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bandv"></a>[BANDV](routine-details.md#routine-bandv) | Eigenvalue problems | user_callable | Form the eigenvectors of a real symmetric band matrix associated with a set of ordered approximate eigenvalues by inverse iteration. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bcrh"></a>[BCRH](routine-details.md#routine-bcrh) | FISHPACK elliptic PDE solvers | subsidiary | Subsidiary to CBLKTR | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bdiff"></a>[BDIFF](routine-details.md#routine-bdiff) | Special functions | subsidiary | Subsidiary to BSKIN | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-besi"></a>[BESI](routine-details.md#routine-besi) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute an N member sequence of I Bessel functions I/SUB(ALPHA+K-1)/(X), K=1,...,N or scaled Bessel functions EXP(-X)*I/SUB(ALPHA+K-1)/(X), K=1,...,N for non-negative ALPHA and X. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-besi0"></a>[BESI0](routine-details.md#routine-besi0) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute the hyperbolic Bessel function of the first kind of order zero. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-besi0e"></a>[BESI0E](routine-details.md#routine-besi0e) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute the exponentially scaled modified (hyperbolic) Bessel function of the first kind of order zero. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-besi1"></a>[BESI1](routine-details.md#routine-besi1) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute the modified (hyperbolic) Bessel function of the first kind of order one. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-besi1e"></a>[BESI1E](routine-details.md#routine-besi1e) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute the exponentially scaled modified (hyperbolic) Bessel function of the first kind of order one. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-besj"></a>[BESJ](routine-details.md#routine-besj) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute an N member sequence of J Bessel functions J/SUB(ALPHA+K-1)/(X), K=1,...,N for non-negative ALPHA and X. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-besj0"></a>[BESJ0](routine-details.md#routine-besj0) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute the Bessel function of the first kind of order zero. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-besj1"></a>[BESJ1](routine-details.md#routine-besj1) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute the Bessel function of the first kind of order one. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-besk"></a>[BESK](routine-details.md#routine-besk) | Special functions | user_callable | Implement forward recursion on the three term recursion relation for a sequence of non-negative order Bessel functions K/SUB(FNU+I-1)/(X), or scaled Bessel functions EXP(X)*K/SUB(FNU+I-1)/(X), I=1,...,N for real, positive X and non-negative orders FNU. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-besk0"></a>[BESK0](routine-details.md#routine-besk0) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute the modified (hyperbolic) Bessel function of the third kind of order zero. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-besk0e"></a>[BESK0E](routine-details.md#routine-besk0e) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute the exponentially scaled modified (hyperbolic) Bessel function of the third kind of order zero. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-besk1"></a>[BESK1](routine-details.md#routine-besk1) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute the modified (hyperbolic) Bessel function of the third kind of order one. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-besk1e"></a>[BESK1E](routine-details.md#routine-besk1e) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute the exponentially scaled modified (hyperbolic) Bessel function of the third kind of order one. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-beskes"></a>[BESKES](routine-details.md#routine-beskes) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute a sequence of exponentially scaled modified Bessel functions of the third kind of fractional order. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-besknu"></a>[BESKNU](routine-details.md#routine-besknu) | Special functions | subsidiary | Subsidiary to BESK | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-besks"></a>[BESKS](routine-details.md#routine-besks) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute a sequence of modified Bessel functions of the third kind of fractional order. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-besy"></a>[BESY](routine-details.md#routine-besy) | Special functions | user_callable | Implement forward recursion on the three term recursion relation for a sequence of non-negative order Bessel functions Y/SUB(FNU+I-1)/(X), I=1,...,N for real, positive X and non-negative orders FNU. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-besy0"></a>[BESY0](routine-details.md#routine-besy0) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute the Bessel function of the second kind of order zero. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-besy1"></a>[BESY1](routine-details.md#routine-besy1) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute the Bessel function of the second kind of order one. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-besynu"></a>[BESYNU](routine-details.md#routine-besynu) | Special functions | subsidiary | Subsidiary to BESY | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-beta"></a>[BETA](routine-details.md#routine-beta) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute the complete Beta function. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-betai"></a>[BETAI](routine-details.md#routine-betai) | Special functions | user_callable | Calculate the incomplete Beta function. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-bfqad"></a>[BFQAD](routine-details.md#routine-bfqad) | Numerical quadrature | user_callable | Compute the integral of a product of a function and a derivative of a B-spline. | source: canonical_verified; raw: not_bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bi"></a>[BI](routine-details.md#routine-bi) | Special functions | user_callable | Evaluate the Bairy function (the Airy function of the second kind). | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-bie"></a>[BIE](routine-details.md#routine-bie) | Special functions | user_callable | Calculate the Bairy function for a negative argument and an exponentially scaled Bairy function for a non-negative argument. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-binom"></a>[BINOM](routine-details.md#routine-binom) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute the binomial coefficients. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-bint4"></a>[BINT4](routine-details.md#routine-bint4) | Interpolation | user_callable | Compute the B-representation of a cubic spline which interpolates given data. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bintk"></a>[BINTK](routine-details.md#routine-bintk) | Interpolation | user_callable | Compute the B-representation of a spline which interpolates given data. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-bisect"></a>[BISECT](routine-details.md#routine-bisect) | Eigenvalue problems | user_callable | Compute the eigenvalues of a symmetric tridiagonal matrix in a given interval using Sturm sequencing. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bkias"></a>[BKIAS](routine-details.md#routine-bkias) | Special functions | subsidiary | Subsidiary to BSKIN | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bkisr"></a>[BKISR](routine-details.md#routine-bkisr) | Special functions | subsidiary | Subsidiary to BSKIN | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bksol"></a>[BKSOL](routine-details.md#routine-bksol) | ODE solvers | subsidiary | Subsidiary to BVSUP | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-blktr1"></a>[BLKTR1](routine-details.md#routine-blktr1) | FISHPACK elliptic PDE solvers | subsidiary | Subsidiary to BLKTRI | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-blktri"></a>[BLKTRI](routine-details.md#routine-blktri) | FISHPACK elliptic PDE solvers | user_callable | Solve a block tridiagonal system of linear equations (usually resulting from the discretization of separable two-dimensional elliptic equations). | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bndacc"></a>[BNDACC](routine-details.md#routine-bndacc) | Dense linear algebra | user_callable | Compute the LU factorization of a banded matrices using sequential accumulation of rows of the data matrix. Exactly one right-hand side vector is permitted. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bndsol"></a>[BNDSOL](routine-details.md#routine-bndsol) | Dense linear algebra | user_callable | Solve the least squares problem for a banded matrix using sequential accumulation of rows of the data matrix. Exactly one right-hand side vector is permitted. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bnfac"></a>[BNFAC](routine-details.md#routine-bnfac) | Interpolation | subsidiary | Subsidiary to BINT4 and BINTK | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bnslv"></a>[BNSLV](routine-details.md#routine-bnslv) | Interpolation | subsidiary | Subsidiary to BINT4 and BINTK | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bqr"></a>[BQR](routine-details.md#routine-bqr) | Eigenvalue problems | user_callable | Compute some of the eigenvalues of a real symmetric matrix using the QR method with shifts of origin. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bsgq8"></a>[BSGQ8](routine-details.md#routine-bsgq8) | Numerical quadrature | subsidiary | Subsidiary to BFQAD | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bskin"></a>[BSKIN](routine-details.md#routine-bskin) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute repeated integrals of the K-zero Bessel function. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bspdoc"></a>[BSPDOC](routine-details.md#routine-bspdoc) | Interpolation | user_callable | Documentation for BSPLINE, a package of subprograms for working with piecewise polynomial functions in B-representation. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bspdr"></a>[BSPDR](routine-details.md#routine-bspdr) | Interpolation | user_callable | Use the B-representation to construct a divided difference table preparatory to a (right) derivative calculation. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bspev"></a>[BSPEV](routine-details.md#routine-bspev) | Interpolation | user_callable | Calculate the value of the spline and its derivatives from the B-representation. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bsplvd"></a>[BSPLVD](routine-details.md#routine-bsplvd) | Approximation | subsidiary | Subsidiary to FC | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bsplvn"></a>[BSPLVN](routine-details.md#routine-bsplvn) | Approximation | subsidiary | Subsidiary to FC | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bsppp"></a>[BSPPP](routine-details.md#routine-bsppp) | Interpolation | user_callable | Convert the B-representation of a B-spline to the piecewise polynomial (PP) form. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-bspvd"></a>[BSPVD](routine-details.md#routine-bspvd) | Interpolation | user_callable | Calculate the value and all derivatives of order less than NDERIV of all basis functions which do not vanish at X. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bspvn"></a>[BSPVN](routine-details.md#routine-bspvn) | Interpolation | user_callable | Calculate the value of all (possibly) nonzero basis functions at X. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bsqad"></a>[BSQAD](routine-details.md#routine-bsqad) | Numerical quadrature | user_callable | Compute the integral of a K-th order B-spline using the B-representation. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-bsrh"></a>[BSRH](routine-details.md#routine-bsrh) | FISHPACK elliptic PDE solvers | subsidiary | Subsidiary to BLKTRI | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bvalu"></a>[BVALU](routine-details.md#routine-bvalu) | Interpolation | user_callable | Evaluate the B-representation of a B-spline at X for the function value or any of its derivatives. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: safe_public |
| <a id="routine-bvder"></a>[BVDER](routine-details.md#routine-bvder) | ODE solvers | subsidiary | Subsidiary to BVSUP | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bvpor"></a>[BVPOR](routine-details.md#routine-bvpor) | ODE solvers | subsidiary | Subsidiary to BVSUP | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-bvsup"></a>[BVSUP](routine-details.md#routine-bvsup) | ODE solvers | user_callable | Solve a linear two-point boundary value problem using superposition coupled with an orthonormalization procedure and a variable-step integration scheme. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |

## <a id="alpha-c"></a>C

| Routine | Family | Role | Purpose | Coverage |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| <a id="routine-c0lgmc"></a>[C0LGMC](routine-details.md#routine-c0lgmc) | Special functions | user_callable | Evaluate (Z+0.5)*LOG((Z+1.)/Z) - 1.0 with relative accuracy. | source: provider_present; raw: not_bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-c1merg"></a>[C1MERG](routine-details.md#routine-c1merg) | Shared numerical utilities | subsidiary | Merge two strings of complex numbers. Each string is ascending by the real part. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-c9lgmc"></a>[C9LGMC](routine-details.md#routine-c9lgmc) | Special functions | subsidiary | Compute the log gamma correction factor so that LOG(CGAMMA(Z)) = 0.5*LOG(2.*PI) + (Z-0.5)*LOG(Z) - Z + C9LGMC(Z). | source: provider_present; raw: not_bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-c9ln2r"></a>[C9LN2R](routine-details.md#routine-c9ln2r) | Elementary and transcendental functions | subsidiary | Evaluate LOG(1+Z) from second order relative accuracy so that LOG(1+Z) = Z - Z**2/2 + Z**3*C9LN2R(Z). | source: provider_present; raw: not_bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-cabs"></a>[CABS](routine-details.md#routine-cabs) | Elementary and transcendental functions | source_only_unclassified | Compute the absolute value of a complex number. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-cacai"></a>[CACAI](routine-details.md#routine-cacai) | Special functions | subsidiary | Subsidiary to CAIRY | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-cacon"></a>[CACON](routine-details.md#routine-cacon) | Special functions | subsidiary | Subsidiary to CBESH and CBESK | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-cacos"></a>[CACOS](routine-details.md#routine-cacos) | Elementary and transcendental functions | user_callable | Compute the complex arc cosine. | source: provider_present; raw: not_bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-cacosh"></a>[CACOSH](routine-details.md#routine-cacosh) | Elementary and transcendental functions | user_callable | Compute the arc hyperbolic cosine. | source: provider_present; raw: not_bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-cairy"></a>[CAIRY](routine-details.md#routine-cairy) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute the Airy function Ai(z) or its derivative dAi/dz for complex argument z. A scaling option is available to help avoid underflow and overflow. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-carg"></a>[CARG](routine-details.md#routine-carg) | Arithmetic and extended-range arithmetic | user_callable | Compute the argument of a complex number. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-casin"></a>[CASIN](routine-details.md#routine-casin) | Elementary and transcendental functions | user_callable | Compute the complex arc sine. | source: provider_present; raw: not_bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-casinh"></a>[CASINH](routine-details.md#routine-casinh) | Elementary and transcendental functions | user_callable | Compute the arc hyperbolic sine. | source: provider_present; raw: not_bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-casyi"></a>[CASYI](routine-details.md#routine-casyi) | Special functions | subsidiary | Subsidiary to CBESI and CBESK | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-catan"></a>[CATAN](routine-details.md#routine-catan) | Elementary and transcendental functions | user_callable | Compute the complex arc tangent. | source: provider_present; raw: not_bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-catan2"></a>[CATAN2](routine-details.md#routine-catan2) | Elementary and transcendental functions | user_callable | Compute the complex arc tangent in the proper quadrant. | source: provider_present; raw: not_bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-catanh"></a>[CATANH](routine-details.md#routine-catanh) | Elementary and transcendental functions | user_callable | Compute the arc hyperbolic tangent. | source: provider_present; raw: not_bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-caxpy"></a>[CAXPY](routine-details.md#routine-caxpy) | Linear algebra kernels | user_callable | Compute a constant times a vector plus a vector. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-cbabk2"></a>[CBABK2](routine-details.md#routine-cbabk2) | Eigenvalue problems | user_callable | Form the eigenvectors of a complex general matrix from the eigenvectors of matrix output from CBAL. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-cbal"></a>[CBAL](routine-details.md#routine-cbal) | Eigenvalue problems | user_callable | Balance a complex general matrix and isolate eigenvalues whenever possible. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-cbesh"></a>[CBESH](routine-details.md#routine-cbesh) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute a sequence of the Hankel functions H(m,a,z) for superscript m=1 or 2, real nonnegative orders a=b, b+1,... where b>0, and nonzero complex argument z. A scaling option is available to help avoid overflow. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |

CDRIV2 allows complex-valued differential equations. | source: canonical_verified; raw: not_bound; safe: none |

This subroutine calculates initial values of P or Q using power series, then performs forward nu-wise recurrence to obtain P(-MU,NU,X), Q(0,NU,X), or Q(1,NU,X). The nu-wise recurrence is stable for P for all mu and for Q for mu=0,1. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |

| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |

| <a id="routine-qcheb"></a>[QCHEB](routine-details.md#routine-qcheb) | Numerical quadrature | subsidiary | This routine computes the CHEBYSHEV series expansion of degrees 12 and 24 of a function using A FAST FOURIER TRANSFORM METHOD F(X) = SUM(K=1,..,13) (CHEB12(K)*T(K-1,X)), F(X) = SUM(K=1,..,25) (CHEB24(K)*T(K-1,X)), Where T(K,X) is the CHEBYSHEV POLYNOMIAL OF DEGREE K. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-qelg"></a>[QELG](routine-details.md#routine-qelg) | Numerical quadrature | subsidiary | The routine determines the limit of a given sequence of approximations, by means of the Epsilon algorithm of P. Wynn. An estimate of the absolute error is also given. The condensed Epsilon table is computed. Usually followed by QZIT, QZVAL, QZVEC. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-qzit"></a>[QZIT](routine-details.md#routine-qzit) | Eigenvalue problems | user_callable | The second step of the QZ algorithm for generalized eigenproblems. Accepts an upper Hessenberg and an upper triangular matrix and reduces the former to quasi-triangular form while preserving the form of the latter. Usually preceded by QZHES and followed by QZVAL and QZVEC. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-qzval"></a>[QZVAL](routine-details.md#routine-qzval) | Eigenvalue problems | user_callable | The third step of the QZ algorithm for generalized eigenproblems. Accepts a pair of real matrices, one in quasi-triangular form and the other in upper triangular form and computes the eigenvalues of the associated eigenproblem. Usually preceded by QZHES, QZIT, and followed by QZVEC. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-qzvec"></a>[QZVEC](routine-details.md#routine-qzvec) | Eigenvalue problems | user_callable | The optional fourth step of the QZ algorithm for generalized eigenproblems. Accepts a matrix in quasi-triangular form and another in upper triangular and computes the eigenvectors of the triangular problem and transforms them back to the original coordinates Usually preceded by QZHES, QZIT, and QZVAL. | source: provider_present; raw: bound; safe: none |

| <a id="routine-sepeli"></a>[SEPELI](routine-details.md#routine-sepeli) | FISHPACK elliptic PDE solvers | user_callable | Discretize and solve a second and, optionally, a fourth order finite difference approximation on a uniform grid to the general separable elliptic partial differential equation on a rectangle with any combination of periodic or mixed boundary conditions. SEPELI solves for either the second-order finite difference approximation or a fourth-order approximation to a separable elliptic equation. 2 2 AF(X)*d U/dX + BF(X)*dU/dX + CF(X)*U + 2 2 DF(Y)*d U/dY + EF(Y)*dU/dY + FF(Y)*U = G(X,Y) on a rectangle (X greater than or equal to A and less than or equal to B; Y greater than or equal to C and less than or equal to D). Any combination of periodic or mixed boundary conditions is allowed. The possible boundary conditions are: in the X-direction: (0) Periodic, U(X+B-A,Y)=U(X,Y) for all Y,X (1) U(A,Y), U(B,Y) are specified for all Y (2) U(A,Y), dU(B,Y)/dX+BETA*U(B,Y) are specified for all Y (3) dU(A,Y)/dX+ALPHA*U(A,Y),dU(B,Y)/dX+ BETA*U(B,Y) are specified for all Y (4) dU(A,Y)/dX+ALPHA*U(A,Y),U(B,Y) are specified for all Y in the Y-direction: (0) Periodic, U(X,Y+D-C)=U(X,Y) for all X,Y (1) U(X,C),U(X,D) are specified for all X (2) U(X,C),dU(X,D)/dY+XNU*U(X,D) are specified for all X (3) dU(X,C)/dY+GAMA*U(X,C),dU(X,D)/dY+ XNU*U(X,D) are specified for all X (4) dU(X,C)/dY+GAMA*U(X,C),U(X,D) are specified for all X Arguments On Input INTL = 0 On initial entry to SEPELI or if any of the arguments C, D, N, NBDCND, COFY are changed from a previous call = 1 If C, D, N, NBDCND, COFY are unchanged from the previous call. IORDER = 2 If a second-order approximation is sought = 4 If a fourth-order approximation is sought A,B The range of the X-independent variable; i.e., X is greater than or equal to A and less than or equal to B. A must be less than B. M The number of panels into which the interval [A,B] is subdivided. Hence, there will be M+1 grid points in the X-direction given by XI=A+(I-1)*DLX for I=1,2,...,M+1 where DLX=(B-A)/M is the panel width. M must be less than IDMN and greater than 5. MBDCND Indicates the type of boundary condition at X=A and X=B = 0 If the solution is periodic in X; i.e., U(X+B-A,Y)=U(X,Y) for all Y,X = 1 If the solution is specified at X=A and X=B; i.e., U(A,Y) and U(B,Y) are specified for all Y = 2 If the solution is specified at X=A and the boundary condition is mixed at X=B; i.e., U(A,Y) and dU(B,Y)/dX+BETA*U(B,Y) are specified for all Y = 3 If the boundary conditions at X=A and X=B are mixed; i.e., dU(A,Y)/dX+ALPHA*U(A,Y) and dU(B,Y)/dX+BETA*U(B,Y) are specified for all Y = 4 If the boundary condition at X=A is mixed and the solution is specified at X=B; i.e., dU(A,Y)/dX+ALPHA*U(A,Y) and U(B,Y) are specified for all Y BDA A one-dimensional array of length N+1 that specifies the values of dU(A,Y)/dX+ ALPHA*U(A,Y) at X=A, when MBDCND=3 or 4. BDA(J) = dU(A,YJ)/dX+ALPHA*U(A,YJ); J=1,2,...,N+1 when MBDCND has any other value, BDA is a dummy parameter. On Input ALPHA The scalar multiplying the solution in case of a mixed boundary condition at X=A (see argument BDA). If MBDCND = 3,4 then ALPHA is a dummy parameter. BDB A one-dimensional array of length N+1 that specifies the values of dU(B,Y)/dX+ BETA*U(B,Y) at X=B. When MBDCND=2 or 3 BDB(J) = dU(B,YJ)/dX+BETA*U(B,YJ); J=1,2,...,N+1 When MBDCND has any other value, BDB is a dummy parameter. BETA The scalar multiplying the solution in case of a mixed boundary condition at X=B (see argument BDB). If MBDCND=2,3 then BETA is a dummy parameter. C,D The range of the Y-independent variable; i.e., Y is greater than or equal to C and less than or equal to D. C must be less than D. N The number of panels into which the interval [C,D] is subdivided. Hence, there will be N+1 grid points in the Y-direction given by YJ=C+(J-1)*DLY for J=1,2,...,N+1 where DLY=(D-C)/N is the panel width. In addition, N must be greater than 4. NBDCND Indicates the types of boundary conditions at Y=C and Y=D = 0 If the solution is periodic in Y; i.e., U(X,Y+D-C)=U(X,Y) for all X,Y = 1 If the solution is specified at Y=C and Y = D, i.e., U(X,C) and U(X,D) are specified for all X = 2 If the solution is specified at Y=C and the boundary condition is mixed at Y=D; i.e., U(X,C) and dU(X,D)/dY+XNU*U(X,D) are specified for all X = 3 If the boundary conditions are mixed at Y=C and Y=D; i.e., dU(X,D)/dY+GAMA*U(X,C) and dU(X,D)/dY+XNU*U(X,D) are specified for all X = 4 If the boundary condition is mixed at Y=C and the solution is specified at Y=D; i.e. dU(X,C)/dY+GAMA*U(X,C) and U(X,D) are specified for all X BDC A one-dimensional array of length M+1 that specifies the value of dU(X,C)/dY+GAMA*U(X,C) at Y=C. When NBDCND=3 or 4 BDC(I) = dU(XI,C)/dY + GAMA*U(XI,C); I=1,2,...,M+1. When NBDCND has any other value, BDC is a dummy parameter. GAMA The scalar multiplying the solution in case of a mixed boundary condition at Y=C (see argument BDC). If NBDCND=3,4 then GAMA is a dummy parameter. BDD A one-dimensional array of length M+1 that specifies the value of dU(X,D)/dY + XNU*U(X,D) at Y=C. When NBDCND=2 or 3 BDD(I) = dU(XI,D)/dY + XNU*U(XI,D); I=1,2,...,M+1. When NBDCND has any other value, BDD is a dummy parameter. XNU The scalar multiplying the solution in case of a mixed boundary condition at Y=D (see argument BDD). If NBDCND=2 or 3 then XNU is a dummy parameter. COFX A user-supplied subprogram with parameters X, AFUN, BFUN, CFUN which returns the values of the X-dependent coefficients AF(X), BF(X), CF(X) in the elliptic equation at X. COFY A user-supplied subprogram with parameters Y, DFUN, EFUN, FFUN which returns the values of the Y-dependent coefficients DF(Y), EF(Y), FF(Y) in the elliptic equation at Y. NOTE: COFX and COFY must be declared external in the calling routine. The values returned in AFUN and DFUN must satisfy AFUN*DFUN greater than 0 for A less than X less than B, C less than Y less than D (see IERROR=10). The coefficients provided may lead to a matrix equation which is not diagonally dominant in which case solution may fail (see IERROR=4). GRHS A two-dimensional array that specifies the values of the right-hand side of the elliptic equation; i.e., GRHS(I,J)=G(XI,YI), for I=2,...,M; J=2,...,N. At the boundaries, GRHS is defined by MBDCND GRHS(1,J) GRHS(M+1,J) ------ --------- ----------0 G(A,YJ) G(B,YJ) 1 * * 2 * G(B,YJ) J=1,2,...,N+1 3 G(A,YJ) G(B,YJ) 4 G(A,YJ) * NBDCND GRHS(I,1) GRHS(I,N+1) ------ --------- ----------0 G(XI,C) G(XI,D) 1 * * 2 * G(XI,D) I=1,2,...,M+1 3 G(XI,C) G(XI,D) 4 G(XI,C) * where * means these quantities are not used. GRHS should be dimensioned IDMN by at least N+1 in the calling routine. USOL A two-dimensional array that specifies the values of the solution along the boundaries. At the boundaries, USOL is defined by MBDCND USOL(1,J) USOL(M+1,J) ------ --------- ----------0 * * 1 U(A,YJ) U(B,YJ) 2 U(A,YJ) * J=1,2,...,N+1 3 * * 4 * U(B,YJ) NBDCND USOL(I,1) USOL(I,N+1) ------ --------- ----------0 * * 1 U(XI,C) U(XI,D) 2 U(XI,C) * I=1,2,...,M+1 3 * * 4 * U(XI,D) where * means the quantities are not used in the solution. If IORDER=2, the user may equivalence GRHS and USOL to save space. Note that in this case the tables specifying the boundaries of the GRHS and USOL arrays determine the boundaries uniquely except at the corners. If the tables call for both G(X,Y) and U(X,Y) at a corner then the solution must be chosen. For example, if MBDCND=2 and NBDCND=4, then U(A,C), U(A,D), U(B,D) must be chosen at the corners in addition to G(B,C). If IORDER=4, then the two arrays, USOL and GRHS, must be distinct. USOL should be dimensioned IDMN by at least N+1 in the calling routine. IDMN The row (or first) dimension of the arrays GRHS and USOL as it appears in the program calling SEPELI. This parameter is used to specify the variable dimension of GRHS and USOL. IDMN must be at least 7 and greater than or equal to M+1. W A one-dimensional array that must be provided by the user for work space. Let K=INT(log2(N+1))+1 and set L=2**(K+1). then (K-2)*L+K+10*N+12*M+27 will suffice as a length of W. THE actual length of W in the calling routine must be set in W(1) (see IERROR=11). On Output USOL Contains the approximate solution to the elliptic equation. USOL(I,J) is the approximation to U(XI,YJ) for I=1,2...,M+1 and J=1,2,...,N+1. The approximation has error O(DLX**2+DLY**2) if called with IORDER=2 and O(DLX**4+DLY**4) if called with IORDER=4. W Contains intermediate values that must not be destroyed if SEPELI is called again with INTL=1. In addition W(1) contains the exact minimal length (in floating point) required for the work space (see IERROR=11). PERTRB If a combination of periodic or derivative boundary conditions (i.e., ALPHA=BETA=0 if MBDCND=3; GAMA=XNU=0 if NBDCND=3) is specified and if the coefficients of U(X,Y) in the separable elliptic equation are zero (i.e., CF(X)=0 for X greater than or equal to A and less than or equal to B; FF(Y)=0 for Y greater than or equal to C and less than or equal to D) then a solution may not exist. PERTRB is a constant calculated and subtracted from the right-hand side of the matrix equations generated by SEPELI which insures that a solution exists. SEPELI then computes this solution which is a weighted minimal least squares solution to the original problem. IERROR An error flag that indicates invalid input parameters or failure to find a solution = 0 No error = 1 If A greater than B or C greater than D = 2 If MBDCND less than 0 or MBDCND greater than 4 = 3 If NBDCND less than 0 or NBDCND greater than 4 = 4 If attempt to find a solution fails. (the linear system generated is not diagonally dominant.) = 5 If IDMN is too small (see discussion of IDMN) = 6 If M is too small or too large (see discussion of M) = 7 If N is too small (see discussion of N) = 8 If IORDER is not 2 or 4 = 9 If INTL is not 0 or 1 = 10 If AFUN*DFUN less than or equal to 0 for some interior mesh point (XI,YJ) = 11 If the work space length input in W(1) is less than the exact minimal work space length required output in W(1). NOTE (concerning IERROR=4): for the coefficients input through COFX, COFY, the discretization may lead to a block tridiagonal linear system which is not diagonally dominant (for example, this happens if CFUN=0 and BFUN/(2.*DLX) greater than AFUN/DLX**2). In this case solution may fail. This cannot happen in the limit as DLX, DLY approach zero. Hence, the condition may be remedied by taking larger values for M or N. Entry Points SEPELI, SPELIP, CHKPRM, CHKSNG, ORTHOG, MINSOL, TRISP, DEFER, DX, DY, BLKTRI, BLKTR1, INDXB, INDXA, INDXC, PROD, PRODP, CPROD, CPRODP, PPADD, PSGF, BSRH, PPSGF, PPSPF, COMPB, TRUN1, STOR1, TQLRAT Special Conditions NONE Common Blocks SPLP, CBLKT I/O NONE Precision Single Specialist John C. Adams, NCAR, Boulder, Colorado 80307 Language FORTRAN History Developed at NCAR during 1975-76. Algorithm SEPELI automatically discretizes the separable elliptic equation which is then solved by a generalized cyclic reduction algorithm in the subroutine, BLKTRI. The fourth-order solution is obtained using 'Deferred Corrections' which is described and referenced in sections, | source: provider_present; raw: not_bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-sepx4"></a>[SEPX4](routine-details.md#routine-sepx4) | FISHPACK elliptic PDE solvers | user_callable | Solve for either the second or fourth order finite difference approximation to the solution of a separable elliptic partial differential equation on a rectangle. Any combination of periodic or mixed boundary conditions is allowed. SEPX4 solves for either the second-order finite difference approximation or a fourth-order approximation to the solution of a separable elliptic equation AF(X)*UXX+BF(X)*UX+CF(X)*U+UYY = G(X,Y) on a rectangle (X greater than or equal to A and less than or equal to B; Y greater than or equal to C and less than or equal to D). Any combination of periodic or mixed boundary conditions is allowed. If boundary conditions in the X direction are periodic (see MBDCND=0 below) then the coefficients must satisfy AF(X)=C1,BF(X)=0,CF(X)=C2 for all X. Here C1,C2 are constants, C1.GT.0. The possible boundary conditions are in the X-direction: (0) Periodic, U(X+B-A,Y)=U(X,Y) for all Y,X (1) U(A,Y), U(B,Y) are specified for all Y (2) U(A,Y), dU(B,Y)/dX+BETA*U(B,Y) are specified for all Y (3) dU(A,Y)/dX+ALPHA*U(A,Y),dU(B,Y)/dX+ BETA*U(B,Y) are specified for all Y (4) dU(A,Y)/dX+ALPHA*U(A,Y),U(B,Y) are specified for all Y In the Y-direction: (0) Periodic, U(X,Y+D-C)=U(X,Y) for all X,Y (1) U(X,C),U(X,D) are specified for all X (2) U(X,C),dU(X,D)/dY are specified for all X (3) dU(X,C)/DY,dU(X,D)/dY are specified for all X (4) dU(X,C)/DY,U(X,D) are specified for all X Usage Call SEPX4(IORDER,A,B,M,MBDCND,BDA,ALPHA,BDB, BETA,C,D,N,NBDCND,BDC,BDD,COFX, GRHS,USOL,IDMN,W,PERTRB,IERROR) Arguments IORDER = 2 If a second-order approximation is sought = 4 If a fourth-order approximation is sought A,B The range of the X-independent variable; i.e., X is greater than or equal to A and less than or equal to B. A must be less than B. M The number of panels into which the interval [A,B] is subdivided. Hence, there will be M+1 grid points in the X-direction given by XI=A+(I-1)*DLX for I=1,2,...,M+1 where DLX=(B-A)/M is the panel width. M must be less than IDMN and greater than 5. MBDCND Indicates the type of boundary condition at X=A and X=B = 0 If the solution is periodic in X; i.e., U(X+B-A,Y)=U(X,Y) for all Y,X = 1 If the solution is specified at X=A and X=B; i.e., U(A,Y) and U(B,Y) are specified for all Y = 2 If the solution is specified at X=A and the boundary condition is mixed at X=B; i.e., U(A,Y) and dU(B,Y)/dX+BETA*U(B,Y) are specified for all Y = 3 If the boundary conditions at X=A and X=B are mixed; i.e., dU(A,Y)/dX+ALPHA*U(A,Y) and dU(B,Y)/dX+BETA*U(B,Y) are specified for all Y = 4 If the boundary condition at X=A is mixed and the solution is specified at X=B; i.e., dU(A,Y)/dX+ALPHA*U(A,Y) and U(B,Y) are specified for all Y BDA A one-dimensional array of length N+1 that specifies the values of dU(A,Y)/dX+ ALPHA*U(A,Y) at X=A, when MBDCND=3 or 4. BDA(J) = dU(A,YJ)/dX+ALPHA*U(A,YJ); J=1,2,...,N+1 When MBDCND has any other value, BDA is a dummy parameter. On Input ALPHA The scalar multiplying the solution in case of a mixed boundary condition AT X=A (see argument BDA). If MBDCND = 3,4 then ALPHA is a dummy parameter. BDB A one-dimensional array of length N+1 that specifies the values of dU(B,Y)/dX+ BETA*U(B,Y) at X=B. when MBDCND=2 or 3 BDB(J) = dU(B,YJ)/dX+BETA*U(B,YJ); J=1,2,...,N+1 When MBDCND has any other value, BDB is a dummy parameter. BETA The scalar multiplying the solution in case of a mixed boundary condition at X=B (see argument BDB). If MBDCND=2,3 then BETA is a dummy parameter. C,D The range of the Y-independent variable; i.e., Y is greater than or equal to C and less than or equal to D. C must be less than D. N The number of panels into which the interval [C,D] is subdivided. Hence, there will be N+1 grid points in the Y-direction given by YJ=C+(J-1)*DLY for J=1,2,...,N+1 where DLY=(D-C)/N is the panel width. In addition, N must be greater than 4. NBDCND Indicates the types of boundary conditions at Y=C and Y=D = 0 If the solution is periodic in Y; i.e., U(X,Y+D-C)=U(X,Y) for all X,Y = 1 If the solution is specified at Y=C and Y = D, i.e., U(X,C) and U(X,D) are specified for all X = 2 If the solution is specified at Y=C and the boundary condition is mixed at Y=D; i.e., dU(X,C)/dY and U(X,D) are specified for all X = 3 If the boundary conditions are mixed at Y= C and Y=D i.e., dU(X,D)/DY and dU(X,D)/dY are specified for all X = 4 If the boundary condition is mixed at Y=C and the solution is specified at Y=D; i.e. dU(X,C)/dY+GAMA*U(X,C) and U(X,D) are specified for all X BDC A one-dimensional array of length M+1 that specifies the value dU(X,C)/DY at Y=C. When NBDCND=3 or 4 BDC(I) = dU(XI,C)/DY I=1,2,...,M+1. When NBDCND has any other value, BDC is a dummy parameter. BDD A one-dimensional array of length M+1 that specifies the value of dU(X,D)/DY at Y=D. When NBDCND=2 or 3 BDD(I)=dU(XI,D)/DY I=1,2,...,M+1. When NBDCND has any other value, BDD is a dummy parameter. COFX A user-supplied subprogram with parameters X, AFUN, BFUN, CFUN which returns the values of the X-dependent coefficients AF(X), BF(X), CF(X) in the elliptic equation at X. If boundary conditions in the X direction are periodic then the coefficients must satisfy AF(X)=C1,BF(X)=0,CF(X)=C2 for all X. Here C1.GT.0 and C2 are constants. Note that COFX must be declared external in the calling routine. GRHS A two-dimensional array that specifies the values of the right-hand side of the elliptic equation; i.e., GRHS(I,J)=G(XI,YI), for I=2,...,M; J=2,...,N. At the boundaries, GRHS is defined by MBDCND GRHS(1,J) GRHS(M+1,J) ------ --------- ----------0 G(A,YJ) G(B,YJ) 1 * * 2 * G(B,YJ) J=1,2,...,N+1 3 G(A,YJ) G(B,YJ) 4 G(A,YJ) * NBDCND GRHS(I,1) GRHS(I,N+1) ------ --------- ----------0 G(XI,C) G(XI,D) 1 * * 2 * G(XI,D) I=1,2,...,M+1 3 G(XI,C) G(XI,D) 4 G(XI,C) * where * means these quantities are not used. GRHS should be dimensioned IDMN by at least N+1 in the calling routine. USOL A two-dimensional array that specifies the values of the solution along the boundaries. At the boundaries, USOL is defined by MBDCND USOL(1,J) USOL(M+1,J) ------ --------- ----------0 * * 1 U(A,YJ) U(B,YJ) 2 U(A,YJ) * J=1,2,...,N+1 3 * * 4 * U(B,YJ) NBDCND USOL(I,1) USOL(I,N+1) ------ --------- ----------0 * * 1 U(XI,C) U(XI,D) 2 U(XI,C) * I=1,2,...,M+1 3 * * 4 * U(XI,D) where * means the quantities are not used in the solution. If IORDER=2, the user may equivalence GRHS and USOL to save space. Note that in this case the tables specifying the boundaries of the GRHS and USOL arrays determine the boundaries uniquely except at the corners. If the tables call for both G(X,Y) and U(X,Y) at a corner then the solution must be chosen. For example, if MBDCND=2 and NBDCND=4, then U(A,C), U(A,D), U(B,D) must be chosen at the corners in addition to G(B,C). If IORDER=4, then the two arrays, USOL and GRHS, must be distinct. USOL should be dimensioned IDMN by at least N+1 in the calling routine. IDMN The row (or first) dimension of the arrays GRHS and USOL as it appears in the program calling SEPX4. This parameter is used to specify the variable dimension of GRHS and USOL. IDMN must be at least 7 and greater than or equal to M+1. W A one-dimensional array that must be provided by the user for work space. 10*N+(16+INT(log2(N)))*(M+1)+23 will suffice as a length for W. The actual length of W in the calling routine must be set in W(1) (see IERROR=11). On Output USOL Contains the approximate solution to the elliptic equation. USOL(I,J) is the approximation to U(XI,YJ) for I=1,2...,M+1 and J=1,2,...,N+1. The approximation has error O(DLX**2+DLY**2) if called with IORDER=2 and O(DLX**4+DLY**4) if called with IORDER=4. W W(1) contains the exact minimal length (in floating point) required for the work space (see IERROR=11). PERTRB If a combination of periodic or derivative boundary conditions (i.e., ALPHA=BETA=0 if MBDCND=3) is specified and if CF(X)=0 for all X, then a solution to the discretized matrix equation may not exist (reflecting the nonuniqueness of solutions to the PDE). PERTRB is a constant calculated and subtracted from the right hand side of the matrix equation insuring the existence of a solution. SEPX4 computes this solution which is a weighted minimal least squares solution to the original problem. If singularity is not detected PERTRB=0.0 is returned by SEPX4. IERROR An error flag that indicates invalid input parameters or failure to find a solution = 0 No error = 1 If A greater than B or C greater than D = 2 If MBDCND less than 0 or MBDCND greater than 4 = 3 If NBDCND less than 0 or NBDCND greater than 4 = 4 If attempt to find a solution fails. (the linear system generated is not diagonally dominant.) = 5 If IDMN is too small (see discussion of IDMN) = 6 If M is too small or too large (see discussion of M) = 7 If N is too small (see discussion of N) = 8 If IORDER is not 2 or 4 = 10 If AFUN is less than or equal to zero for some interior mesh point XI = 11 If the work space length input in W(1) is less than the exact minimal work space length required output in W(1). = 12 If MBDCND=0 and AF(X)=CF(X)=constant or BF(X)=0 for all X is not true. *Long Description: Dimension of BDA(N+1), BDB(N+1), BDC(M+1), BDD(M+1), Arguments USOL(IDMN,N+1), GRHS(IDMN,N+1), W (see argument list) Latest Revision October 1980 Special Conditions NONE Common Blocks SPL4 I/O NONE Precision Single Required Library NONE Files Specialist John C. Adams, NCAR, Boulder, Colorado 80307 Language FORTRAN Entry Points SEPX4,SPELI4,CHKPR4,CHKSN4,ORTHO4,MINSO4,TRIS4, DEFE4,DX4,DY4 History SEPX4 was developed by modifying the ULIB routine SEPELI during October 1978. It should be used instead of SEPELI whenever possible. The increase in speed is at least a factor of three. Algorithm SEPX4 automatically discretizes the separable elliptic equation which is then solved by a generalized cyclic reduction algorithm in the subroutine POIS. The fourth order solution is obtained using the technique of deferred corrections referenced below. | source: provider_present; raw: not_bound; safe: none |

| <a id="routine-zbesi"></a>[ZBESI](routine-details.md#routine-zbesi) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute a sequence of the Bessel functions I(a,z) for complex argument z and real nonnegative orders a=b,b+1, b+2,... where b>0. A scaling option is available to help avoid overflow. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-zbesj"></a>[ZBESJ](routine-details.md#routine-zbesj) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute a sequence of the Bessel functions J(a,z) for complex argument z and real nonnegative orders a=b,b+1, b+2,... where b>0. A scaling option is available to help avoid overflow. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-zbesk"></a>[ZBESK](routine-details.md#routine-zbesk) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute a sequence of the Bessel functions K(a,z) for complex argument z and real nonnegative orders a=b,b+1, b+2,... where b>0. A scaling option is available to help avoid overflow. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
| <a id="routine-zbesy"></a>[ZBESY](routine-details.md#routine-zbesy) | Special functions | user_callable | Compute a sequence of the Bessel functions Y(a,z) for complex argument z and real nonnegative orders a=b,b+1, b+2,... where b>0. A scaling option is available to help avoid overflow. | source: canonical_verified; raw: bound; safe: none |
